<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:saffier.html>saffier</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">sapphirus</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">σάπφειρος</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">sáppheiros</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.

***saffron.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a> (44718)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">safran</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Medieval Latin">Medieval Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">safrānum</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic" class="extiw" title="w:Arabic">Arabic</a></span> <i class="Arab mention" lang="ar">زَعْفَرَان</i> |  <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ar-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">zaʿfarān</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></strong> (<i>countable and uncountable</i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">saffrons</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>The plant <i>Crocus sativus</i>, a crocus.
<ul><li><b>1611</b>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_James_Version" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:King James Version">King James Version</a> of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Bible">Bible</a></i>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Song_of_Songs" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Song of Songs">Song of <a href = vnd.unilang:songs.html>Songs</a></a> 4.13-14,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Song%20of%20Solomon+4amp;version=KJV">[1]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>Thy plants are an orchard of pomegranates, with pleasant fruits; camphire, with spikenard, spikenard and <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2009</b>, D. H. Sanaeinejad, S. N. Hosseini, <i>Regression <a href = vnd.unilang:models.html>Models</a> for <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>Saffron</a></b> Yields in Iran</i>, Daoliang Li, Chunjiang <a href = vnd.unilang:zhao.html>Zhao</a> (<a href = vnd.unilang:editors.html>editors</a>), <i>Computer and Computing Technologies in Agriculture II</i>, Volume 1, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com.au/books?id=DybQsneDddYCamp;pg=PA510amp;dq=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ei=mAOHU4PEFJCtkgWF5YGgAQamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;f=false">page 510</a>,
<dl><dd>Usually the maximum temperature for October, November and December in the southern parts of Khorassan–the main <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> growing area of the Iran-does not exceed 20°C, while the minimum temperature reaches 0°C.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>A spice (seasoning) and colouring <a href = vnd.unilang:agent.html>agent</a> made from the stigma and part of the style of the plant, sometimes or formerly also used as a dye and insect repellent.
<dl><dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonym:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">kesar</span></span></dd></dl>
<ul><li><i>c.</i> <b>1610</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Winter%27s_Tale" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Winter | s Tale">The Winter’s Tale</a></i>, Act IV, Scene 3,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.opensourceshakespeare.org/views/plays/play_view.php?WorkID=winterstaleamp;Scope=entireamp;pleasewait=1amp;msg=pl">[2]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>I must have <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> to colour the warden <a href = vnd.unilang:pies.html>pies</a> <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1658</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Muffet" class="extiw" title="w:Thomas Muffet">Thomas Muffet</a>, <i>The Theatre of Insects</i>, [1634, <i>Insectorum sive Minimorum Animalium Theatrum</i>], quoted in <b>2008</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:anna.html>Anna</a> Suranyi, <i>The Genius of the English Nation: Travel Writing and National Identity in Early Modern England</i>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com.au/books?id=DcV8ZE6uz7MCamp;pg=PA118amp;dq=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ei=mAOHU4PEFJCtkgWF5YGgAQamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;f=false">page 117-118</a>,
<dl><dd>The Irish and Ireland people (who are frequently troubled with lice, and such as will fly, as they say, in summer) anoint their <a href = vnd.unilang:shirts.html>shirts</a> with <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b>, and to very good purpose, to drive away the lice, but after six months they wash their <a href = vnd.unilang:shirts.html>shirts</a> again, putting fresh <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> into the lye.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2002</b>,  James A. Duke (editor),  <cite>CRC Handbook of Medicinal <a href = vnd.unilang:spices.html>Spices</a></cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://books.google.com.au/books?id=g_OCl6P0vsYCamp;pg=PA129amp;dq=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ei=mAOHU4PEFJCtkgWF5YGgAQamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;f=false">[3]</a></sup>, page 129:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>Saffron</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> not included in American and British pharmacopoeias, but some Indian medical formulae still include it.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2004</b>,  Melitta Weiss Adamson,  <cite>Food in Medieval Times</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://books.google.com.au/books?id=jtgud2P-EGwCamp;pg=PA15amp;dq=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ei=mAOHU4PEFJCtkgWF5YGgAQamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;f=false">[4]</a></sup>, page 15:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>Saffron</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the stigma of the crocus flower, which <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> harvested by hand, dried, and <a href = vnd.unilang:sold.html>sold</a> either in strands or ground to powder.<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span>Of all the medieval <a href = vnd.unilang:spices.html>spices</a>, <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> the most expensive, which <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> not surprising given that 70,000 flowers only yield one pound of dried stigmas. In the European cookbooks of the late Middle Ages, nearly all of which which reflect refined upper-class dining, <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> ubiquitous.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>2011</b>, Mathew Attokaran, <i>Natural Food Flavors and Colorants</i>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com.au/books?id=9qcvAoMPYW4Camp;pg=RA1-PA87-IA4amp;dq=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ei=mAOHU4PEFJCtkgWF5YGgAQamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22saffron%22%7C%22saffrons%22amp;f=false">unnumbered page</a>,
<dl><dd><b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>Saffron</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> often called the “golden spice.”</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>An orange-yellow colour, the colour of a lion's pelt.
<dl><dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonym:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a> yellow</span></span></dd>
<dd><div class="color-panel"><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a> colour: <span style="background-color:F4C430; display:inline-block; width:80px;"> </span></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>1728</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Thomson_(poet,_born_1834)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:James Thomson (poet, born 1834)">James Thomson</a>, <i>Spring</i>, London: A. <a href = vnd.unilang:millar.html>Millar</a> amp; G. Strahan, p. 18,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/004808172.0001.000">[5]</a></sup>
<dl><dd><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> The stately Ram</dd>
<dd>Shone thro’ the Mead, in native Purple clad,</dd>
<dd>Or <a href = vnd.unilang:milder.html>milder</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>Saffron</a></b> <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1915</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucy_Maud_Montgomery" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Lucy Maud Montgomery"><a href = vnd.unilang:lucy.html>Lucy</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:maud.html>Maud</a> Montgomery</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anne_of_the_Island" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Anne of the Island"><a href = vnd.unilang:anne.html>Anne</a> of the Island</a></i>, Chapter 7,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/51/51-h/51-h.htm">[6]</a></sup>
<dl><dd><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> the <a href = vnd.unilang:girls.html>girls</a> locked up Echo Lodge again and <a href = vnd.unilang:went.html>went</a> away in the <a href = vnd.unilang:perfect.html>perfect</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:half.html>half</a> hour that follows the <a href = vnd.unilang:rose.html>rose</a> and <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> of a winter sunset.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1973</b>,  Anthony Powell,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temporary_Kings" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Temporary Kings">Temporary Kings</a></cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://books.google.com.au/books?id=1vHrhepiZ7MCamp;pg=PA82amp;dq=%22saffrons%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ei=ZkOHU5iBDMWnkgWd8IGoBAamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22saffrons%22amp;f=false">[7]</a></sup>, page 82:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">These colours might have <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> expressly designed—by dissonance as much as harmony—for juxtaposition against those pouring down in brilliant <a href = vnd.unilang:rays.html>rays</a> of light from the Tiepolo; subtle yet penetrating pinks and greys, light blue turning almost to lavender, rich <b>saffrons</b> and cinnamons melting into bronze and gold.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>2011</b>, Seth Hunter, <i>The <a href = vnd.unilang:winds.html>Winds</a> of Folly</i>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com.au/books?id=OKVsPY6RjtgCamp;pg=PT127amp;dq=%22saffrons%22amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ei=ZkOHU5iBDMWnkgWd8IGoBAamp;redir_esc=yv=onepageamp;q=%22saffrons%22amp;f=false">unnumbered page</a>,
<dl><dd>The classical shades of Antiquity <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> the most <a href = vnd.unilang:prevalent.html>prevalent</a>, but along with the Venetian <a href = vnd.unilang:reds.html>reds</a> and Egyptian blues, the <b>saffrons</b> and ochres and indigos, <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> more delicate hues: of pink and cream and lilac, like <a href = vnd.unilang:shells.html>shells</a> littered upon the shore.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_terms">Related <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>terms</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<div class="list-switcher" data-toggle-category="derived terms"><div class="derivedterms term-list ul-column-count" data-column-count="2" style="background-color: F8F8FF;">
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">safflower</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">safranine</span></li></ul></div><div class="list-switcher-element" data-showtext=" show more ▼ " data-hidetext=" show less  " style="display: none;"> </div></div>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjective">Adjective</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>Having an orange-yellow colour.
<dl><dd><i>The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> robe of a Buddhist monk.</i></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>1624</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Heywood" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Thomas Heywood">Thomas Heywood</a>, <i>Gynaikeion: or, Nine Bookes of Various History. Concerninge women inscribed by the names of the nine Muses</i>, London, Book 3, “A Funerall Oade vpon the death of <a href = vnd.unilang:anna.html>Anna</a> Panareta” p. 123,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A03206.0001.001">[8]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>Now <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hymen_(god)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Hymen (god)">Hymen</a></i> change thy <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> weedes</dd>
<dd>To roabe and habit sable:</dd>
<dd>For ioyfull thoughts, vse funerall deedes</dd>
<dd>Since nothing’s firme or stable;</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1794</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ann_Radcliffe" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Ann Radcliffe">Ann Radcliffe</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Mysteries_of_Udolpho" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Mysteries of Udolpho">The <a href = vnd.unilang:mysteries.html>Mysteries</a> of Udolpho</a></i>, London: G.G. amp; J. Robinson, Volume 1, Chapter 9, p. 256,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/004837676.0001.001">[9]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>The sun <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> now set; but, under the dark <a href = vnd.unilang:branches.html>branches</a> of the almond trees, <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> seen the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> glow of the west, spreading beyond the twilight of middle air.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1876</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Eliot" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:George Eliot">George Eliot</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Deronda" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Daniel Deronda"><a href = vnd.unilang:daniel.html>Daniel</a> Deronda</a></i>, Chapter 40,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/cache/epub/7469/pg7469-images.html">[10]</a></sup>
<dl><dd><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> it <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> half-past four, and the gray day <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> dying gloriously, its western <a href = vnd.unilang:clouds.html>clouds</a> all broken into narrowing purple strata before a wide-spreading <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> clearness <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1961</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V._S._Naipaul" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:V. S. Naipaul">V. S. Naipaul</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_House_for_Mr_Biswas" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:A House for Mr Biswas">A House for <a href = vnd.unilang:mr.html>Mr</a> Biswas</a></i>, Part 1, Chapter 2,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://archive.org/details/in.ernet.dli.2015.149342">[11]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>The jacket <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> brown but <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:turned.html>turned</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></b> where it <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> soaked by <a href = vnd.unilang:lal.html>Lal</a>’s sweat.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">saffrons</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">saffroning</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">saffroned</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>To add <a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a> to (a food), for taste, colour etc.
<dl><dd><i><b>saffroned</b> water, <b>saffroned</b> rice</i>.</dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>1559</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Morwen" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Peter Morwen"><a href = vnd.unilang:peter.html>Peter</a> Morwen</a> (translator), <i>The Treasure of Euonymus</i> by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conrad_Gesner" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Conrad Gesner">Conrad Gesner</a>, London: John Day, “Of certain other Aromatical wynes,” p. 407,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A01662.0001.001">[12]</a></sup>
<dl><dd><b>Saffrond</b> wyne bryngeth mirthe, and taketh away Melancholines <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1884</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Browning" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Robert Browning">Robert Browning</a>, “Two Camels” in <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferishtah%27s_Fancies" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Ferishtah | s Fancies">Ferishtah’s Fancies</a></i>, London: Smith, Elder, p. 70,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://archive.org/details/ferishtahsfanc00brow">[13]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>Well-<b>saffroned</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> that barley-soup!</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>To give a <a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a> colour to (something).
<ul><li><b>1593</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Drayton" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Michael Drayton">Michael Drayton</a>, <i>Idea the Shepheards Garland</i>, London: Thomas Woodcocke, Second Eglog, p. 6,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A20823.0001.001">[14]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>My dreadful thoughts <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> drawen vpon my face,</dd>
<dd>In blotted lines with ages iron <a href = vnd.unilang:pen.html>pen</a>,</dd>
<dd>The lothlie morpheu <b>saffroned</b> the place,</dd>
<dd>Where beuties damaske daz’d the eies of <a href = vnd.unilang:men.html>men</a>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><i>c.</i> <b>1594</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Drayton" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Michael Drayton">Michael Drayton</a>, <i>Peirs Gaueston <a href = vnd.unilang:earle.html>Earle</a> of Cornwall His Life, Death, and Fortune</i>, London: Nicholas <a href = vnd.unilang:ling.html>Ling</a> and John <a href = vnd.unilang:busby.html>Busby</a>,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A20834.0001.001">[15]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>Or like the twifold-twynned <i>Geminy</i>,</dd>
<dd>In their star-gilded gyrdle strongly tyed,</dd>
<dd>Chayn’d by their <b>saffrond</b> tresses in the sky,</dd>
<dd>Standing to guard the sun-coche in his pride.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1917</b>, Charles V. H. Roberts, “The Call of the Country” in <i>Collected Poems</i>, New York: The Torch Press, p. 20,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://archive.org/details/collectedpoems00robegoog">[16]</a></sup>
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>We</a> accept the <a href = vnd.unilang:perfect.html>perfect</a> stillness of the ground,</dd>
<dd>And the vision of a sunset-<b>saffroned</b> sea.</dd></dl></li></ul>
<ol><li>To dye (a fabric, garment, etc.) with a saffron-based dye.
<ul><li><b>1580</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Stow" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:John Stow">John Stow</a>, <i>The <a href = vnd.unilang:chronicles.html>Chronicles</a> of England</i>, London: <a href = vnd.unilang:ralph.html>Ralph</a> Newberie, “A briefe Description of Englande, Scotlande, Wales, and Cornwall,” p. 9,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A13043.0001.001">[17]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>The other part Northern, amp; ful of mountaines, a very rude and homely kinde of people doth inhabite, which are called the redshankes or <a href = vnd.unilang:wilde.html>wilde</a> Scottes. They be clothed with a <a href = vnd.unilang:mantel.html>mantel</a> and shyrte <b>saffroned</b>, after the Irishe manner, going bare legged to the knée.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1582</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Stanyhurst" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Richard Stanyhurst">Richard Stanyhurst</a> (translator), <i>The First Foure Bookes of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgil" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Virgil"><a href = vnd.unilang:virgil.html>Virgil</a></a> his <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aeneid" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Aeneid">Aeneis</a></i>, <a href = vnd.unilang:leiden.html>Leiden</a>: John Pates, Book 4, p. 82,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A14485.0001.001">[18]</a></sup>
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:thee.html>Thee</a> next day foloing lustring <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aurora_(mythology)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Aurora (mythology)">Aurora</a> lay shymring,</dd>
<dd>Her <b>saffrond</b> mattresse leauing to her bedfelo <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tithonus" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Tithonus">Tithon</a>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1638</b>, uncredited translator, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:historie.html>Historie</a> Naturall and Experimentall, of Life and Death</i> by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francis_Bacon" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Francis Bacon">Francis Bacon</a>, London: William Lee and Humphrey Mosley, p. 244,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A01454.0001.001">[19]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>The same <i>Irish</i>, use to weare <i><b>Saffroned</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:linnen.html>Linnen</a></i>, and <a href = vnd.unilang:shirts.html>Shirts</a>; Which though it <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a>, at first, devised to prevent Vermine, yet, howsoever, I take it, to be very usefull for Lengthening of Life <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>To colour (a metal or wooden surface) with a gilding product containing <a href = vnd.unilang:saffron.html>saffron</a>.
<ul><li><b>1594</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Nashe" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Thomas Nashe">Thomas Nashe</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Unfortunate_Traveller" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Unfortunate Traveller">The Unfortunate Traveller</a></i>, London: C. Burby,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A08015.0001.001">[20]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>His horse <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> harnished with leaden chaines, hauing the out-side guilt, or at least <b>saffrond</b> in stead of guilt, to decypher a holie or golden pretence of a couetous purpose <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1633</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Donne" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:John Donne">John Donne</a>, “Elegie” in <i>Poems</i>, London: John Marriot, p. 149,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://name.umdl.umich.edu/A69225.0001.001">[21]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>And like vile stones lying in <b>saffrond</b> tinne,</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<ul><li><dl><dd>Or warts, or wheales, it hangs upon her skinne.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">figuratively</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To embellish.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1970</b>,  Robert Randolph Turner,  <cite>Tennessee <a href = vnd.unilang:legends.html>Legends</a>: An Analysis in <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>Terms</a> of Motifs, Structure, and Style</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><b>Saffroning</b> the <a href = vnd.unilang:rest.html>rest</a> of the account are several other regionalisms: agin for against, hit for the expletive it, knowed as a preterite, and no use to say not bin' (a fascinating doubling of the negative).</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1992</b>,  Jerome <a href = vnd.unilang:mandel.html>Mandel</a>,  <cite>Geoffrey Chaucer: Building the Fragments of the Canterbury Tales</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">He <b>saffrons</b> his speech with Latin which he knows all by rote.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b>,  Robert B. Burlin,  <cite>Chaucerian Fiction</cite>, page 231:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The Nun's Priest's rhetorical devices, too numerous to catalogue exhaustively, are of two <a href = vnd.unilang:kinds.html>kinds</a>: first, the heroic-historical, beginning with the setting of the occasion in a time sequence that <a href = vnd.unilang:starts.html>starts</a> with the Creation, <b>saffroning</b> the high points with apostrophes and epic similes, and culminating with a chase in which Chauntecleer's fall proves to have the "cosmic reverberations" required by epic standards <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>

***said.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:said.html>said</a> (11545)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">seide</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="ann-pos">preterite</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">seid</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">iseid</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="ann-pos">past participle</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">sǣde</i>, <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">sæġde</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="ann-pos">preterite</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> and <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">ġesæġd</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="ann-pos">past participle</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, equivalent to <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">say</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">-ed</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>

***sais.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a> (56097)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindi" class="extiw" title="w:Hindi">Hindi</a></span> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindustani_language" class="extiw" title="w:Hindustani language">Hindustani</a>), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic" class="extiw" title="w:Arabic">Arabic</a></span> <i class="Arab mention" lang="ar">سَائِس</i> |  <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ar-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">sāʾis</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">stableman, groom</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <i class="Arab mention" lang="ar">سَاس</i> |  <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ar-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">sās</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to tend a horse</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">saises</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India" class="extiw" title="w:India">India</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A groom, or servant with responsibility for the <a href = vnd.unilang:horses.html>horses</a>.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1808</b>,  Thomas Williamson,  <cite>Oriental Field Sports; being a Complete, Detailed, and Accurate Description of the Wild Sports of the East <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span> In Two <a href = vnd.unilang:volumes.html>Volumes</a></cite>, volume II, London |  Printed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Bulmer_(printer)" class="extiw" title="w:William Bulmer (printer)">W[illiam] Bulmer and Co.</a> Cleveland-Row, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St_James%27s" class="extiw" title="w:St James | s">St. James's</a>; for Edward Orme, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bond_Street" class="extiw" title="w:Bond Street">Bond-Street</a>, the corner of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brook_Street" class="extiw" title="w:Brook Street">Brook-Street</a>, and B. Crosby and Co. Stationers' Court, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/225413285">225413285</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=1BlcAAAAcAAJamp;pg=PA213">page 213</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Not one of them [horse <a href = vnd.unilang:dealers.html>dealers</a>] will venture a horse, he <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> about to sell, in the stables of the intended purchaser, unless attended by one of his own <i><b>syces</b></i>, or grooms, who both knows and <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> known by the animal. If the horse be very old, or naturally dull, the <b>syce</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:takes.html>takes</a> care to ply him with <a href = vnd.unilang:spices.html>spices</a> and other stimulants; and if vicious, opium, and other anodynes are given; so that the horse <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> absolutely in a state of disguise.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>

<dl><dd>THE DUTIES OF THE <i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>Sais</a></b></i> OR GROOM. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> Now, if the good house-mother's proudest boast <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> that not <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>even</a> "the cattle within her gate" fail to feel her kindly care, she will often find it necessary to take an active part in teaching the <i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a></b></i> his duty, and seeing that the <a href = vnd.unilang:horses.html>horses</a> receive proper attention. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> The old plan of a <i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a></b></i> and a grass-cutter to each horse <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a thing of the past, and the number of <i><b>saises</b></i> or grooms should have reference merely to the amount of harnessing and out-work necessary during the day.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1906</b>,  Charles A[tmore] Sherring,  “Superstitions”, in  <cite>Western Tibet and the British Borderland; the Sacred Country of Hindus and Buddhists, with an Account of the Government, Religion, and Customs of its Peoples</cite>, London |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Arnold_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Arnold (publisher)">Edward Arnold</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/3827957">3827957</a></small>, page 100:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">But apart from the story of the havildar, my own <b>syce</b>, a <a href = vnd.unilang:hillman.html>hillman</a> who attends my <a href = vnd.unilang:pony.html>pony</a>, <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> actually seen two <a href = vnd.unilang:ghosts.html>ghosts</a>, with one of whom he <a href = vnd.unilang:held.html>held</a> a long conversation.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>

L. German]: Obtainable from the Malay Information Agency, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterlow_and_Sons" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Waterlow and Sons">Waterlow and Sons</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/27325434">27325434</a></small>, page 50:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">House servants are usually either Chinese or Tamil, the former predominating, especially in <a href = vnd.unilang:towns.html>towns</a> of any size. The domestic staff will in general consist of a houseboy (in large establishments two houseboys), a water carrier (<i>tukang ayer</i>), whose duties include washing dishes and preparing baths, a cook, a gardener, a <a href = vnd.unilang:chauffeur.html>chauffeur</a> or <i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a></b></i>, and perhaps an <i>ayah</i> (if Chinese, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:amah.html>amah</a></i>) or two, <a href = vnd.unilang:according.html>according</a> to the size of the family.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>

The <i><b>syce</b></i>, who <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> squatting down, sheltering in the shade of the car, jumped to his <a href = vnd.unilang:feet.html>feet</a> at their approach, opening the <a href = vnd.unilang:doors.html>doors</a> for them with an efficient flourish.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>

<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2005</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Bayly" class="extiw" title="w:Christopher Bayly">Christopher [Alan] Bayly</a> |  <a href = vnd.unilang:tim.html>Tim</a>[othy <a href = vnd.unilang:norman.html>Norman</a>] Harper,  <cite><a href = vnd.unilang:forgotten.html>Forgotten</a> Armies: The Fall of British Asia, 1941–1945</cite>, Cambridge, Mass. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harvard_University_Press" class="extiw" title="w:Harvard University Press">The Belknap Press of Harvard University Press</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, page 53:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>]he expansion of the service economy, for the home, the office and the municipality, <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> created a more mixed labouring world. A wealthy European or Asian home would bring together a Chinese <i><a href = vnd.unilang:amah.html>amah</a></i>, or maid, a Malay <i><b>syce</b></i>, or <a href = vnd.unilang:chauffeur.html>chauffeur</a>, and an Indian <i>kebun</i>, or gardener, operating through a Malay lingua franca. On a larger scale, in the invisible city, ethnic communities <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:pushed.html>pushed</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:closer.html>closer</a> together, often for the first time.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Nonstandard spelling of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">says</i></span></span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1855</b> August,  “Editor's Drawer”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harper%27s_Magazine" class="extiw" title="w:Harper | s Magazine">Harper's New Monthly Magazine</a></cite>, volume XI, number LXIII, New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harper_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Harper (publisher)">Harper amp; Brothers, Publishers</a>, 329 amp; 331 <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pearl_Street_(Manhattan)" class="extiw" title="w:Pearl Street (Manhattan)">Pearl Street</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_Square_(Manhattan)" class="extiw" title="w:Franklin Square (Manhattan)">Franklin Square</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/1641392">1641392</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=C3cCAAAAIAAJamp;pg=PA425">page 425</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">'Yes,' <b><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a></b> I, 'what's left of <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a>; but, good gracious,' <b><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a></b> I, 'you have got the 'heaves.' I hope it ain'<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> catchin'.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>

Pretty soon camp <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> hunt <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> buffalo, un I <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> hunt Snow-Owl's woman. Every one <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> excite, un dey don' <a href = vnd.unilang:tak.html>tak</a> no 'count of <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a>. I see <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> woman go up leetle coulie for stray horse, un I follar her. I <b><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a></b>, 'How do? You come be my woman. <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>We</a> run off to Meestar MacDonnail's tradehouse.' <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> She <b><a href = vnd.unilang:sais.html>sais</a></b> she afraid.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>

***salade.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a> (4756)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1_2">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_French" class="extiw" title="w:Middle French">Middle French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="frm"><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">salata</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_3">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salades.html>salades</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>saladetje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>salad (a food made primarily of a mixture of raw ingredients, typically vegetables)</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">archaic</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> lettuce
<ul><li><b>1654</b> July 8, Jan <a href = vnd.unilang:van.html>van</a> Riebeeck, <i>Daghregister</i>, part 1, page 238.
<dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:bij.html>Bij</a> welcke missive vernemende <a href = vnd.unilang:hare.html>hare</a> veelvoudige siecken ende grooten noodt <a href = vnd.unilang:om.html>om</a> verversinge, <a href = vnd.unilang:lieten.html>lieten</a> datelijck <a href = vnd.unilang:een.html>een</a> mande <a href = vnd.unilang:met.html>met</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></b> ende 2 <a href = vnd.unilang:goede.html>goede</a> sacken <a href = vnd.unilang:vol.html>vol</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:cool.html>cool</a> gereet maecken, daer se<br />den 9en do., fraij labber uijtte N.<a href = vnd.unilang:westen.html>Westen</a> coelende, 'smorgens vroegh <a href = vnd.unilang:weder.html>weder</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:mede.html>mede</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:na.html>na</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:boort.html>boort</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:sonden.html>sonden</a>, nevens '<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> navolgende briefken, luijdende <a href = vnd.unilang:van.html>van</a> woorde <a href = vnd.unilang:te.html>te</a> woorde <a href = vnd.unilang:als.html>als</a> volcht:</span><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">Learning by means of this missive of their manifold sickpeople and great need for refreshment, [<a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a>] immediately let a basket of <b>lettuce</b> and 2 good <a href = vnd.unilang:bags.html>bags</a> full of cabbage be prepared, so that [<a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a>] / sent them along, on the 9th of the same month, [the wind] <a href = vnd.unilang:blowing.html>blowing</a> rather softly from the North West, on board again in the early morning, beside the following letter, reading word by word as follows:</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_French" class="extiw" title="w:Middle French">Middle French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="frm"><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro"><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_4">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salades.html>salades</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A sallet, a <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></span> <span class="gloss-brac">(</span><span class="gloss-content">certain type of round helmet</span><span class="gloss-brac">)</span>.</li></ol>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zelfstandig_naamwoord"><i><a href = vnd.unilang:zelfstandig.html>Zelfstandig</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:naamwoord.html>naamwoord</a></i></span></h4>
<p><b><a href = vnd.unilang:salade.html>salade</a></b> <span style="background-color: f8f9fa;border-radius: 2px;border: 1px solid c8ccd1;padding: 0 0.2em 0 0.1em;font-style: italic">m</span>/<span style="background-color: f8f9fa;border-radius: 2px;border: 1px solid c8ccd1;padding: 0 0.2em 0 0.1em;font-style: italic">v</span>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:salie.html>salie</a> (40222)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:salie.html>salie</a></i>, from older <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">saelge</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">selge</i>.
</p>

***salto.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:salto.html>salto</a> (18353)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it"><a href = vnd.unilang:salto.html>salto</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">saltus</i>. First attested in the 18th century.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_4">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salto.html>salto</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salto.html>salto</a>'s</b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:salto.html>saltootje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>somersault, flip <span class="gloss-brac">(</span><span class="gloss-content">jump where one <a href = vnd.unilang:makes.html>makes</a> a 360° rotation</span><span class="gloss-brac">)</span> <span class="defdate">[from 19th c.]</span></li></ol>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:salut.html>salut</a> (48550)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_4">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:saluut.html>saluut</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">salūtō</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to greet; to wish health to</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_5">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="id"><a href = vnd.unilang:salut.html>salut</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">salute</span>, an utterance or gesture expressing greeting or honor towards someone, now especially a formal, non-verbal gesture made with the arms or hands in any of various specific positions

***salve.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a> (79842)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">sealf</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*salbō</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*solp-éh₂</i>, from <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*selp-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a>, ointment</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Low_German" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Low German">Middle Low German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gml"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></i> (<span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Danish language">Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="da"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zalf.html>zalf</a></i>), <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">salba</i> (<span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Salbe</i>), <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gothic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Gothic href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit" class="extiw" title="w:Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a></span> <i class="Deva mention" lang="sa">सर्पिस्</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="sa-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">sarpís</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">ἔλπος</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">élpos</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">salves</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>An ointment, cream, or balm with soothing, healing, or calming <a href = vnd.unilang:effects.html>effects</a>.</li>
<li>Any remedy or action that soothes or heals.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">sealfian</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*salbōną</i>, from <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*salbō</i> (whence <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="ann-pos">noun</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>).
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">salves</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">salving</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">salved</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To calm or assuage.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1985</b>,  Joan Morrison,  <cite>Share House Blues</cite>, Boolarong Publications, page 26:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">She <a href = vnd.unilang:feels.html>feels</a> guilty for pampering him, and <b>salves</b> her conscience by bossily ordering him to go and fetch the <a href = vnd.unilang:clothes.html>clothes</a> from the line[.]</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>To heal by applications or medicaments; to apply <a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a> to; to anoint.
<ul><li><b>1591</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a> <i>The First Part of King <a href = vnd.unilang:henry.html>Henry</a> IV</i>:
<dl><dd>I do beseech your majesty . . . <b><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></b> the long-grown wounds of my intemperance."</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>To heal; to remedy; to cure; to make good.
<ul><li><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(Can <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> date this quote by Spenser and provide title, author’s full name, and other <a href = vnd.unilang:details.html>details</a>?)</span>
<dl><dd>But Ebranck <b>salved</b> both their infamies / With noble <a href = vnd.unilang:deeds.html>deeds</a>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1644</b>,  John Milton,  <cite>The Doctrine or Discipline of Divorce</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">What may <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> do, then, to <b><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></b> this seeming inconsistence?</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>To salvage.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">salvō</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to save</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb_2">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">salves</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">salving</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">salved</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete<span class="ib-comma">,</span> astronomy</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To save (the appearances or the phenomena); to explain (a celestial phenomenon); to account for (the apparent motions of the celestial <a href = vnd.unilang:bodies.html>bodies</a>).</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To resolve (a difficulty); to refute (an objection); to harmonize (an apparent contradiction).
<ul><li><b>1661</b>, Thomas Salusbury (translator), <i>Galileo's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dialogue_Concerning_the_Two_Chief_World_Systems" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Dialogue Concerning the Two Chief World Systems">Dialogue Concerning the Two Chief World Systems</a></i>
<dl><dd>He which should hold it more rational to make the whole Universe move, and thereby to <b><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></b> the Earths mobility, <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> more unreasonable....</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To explain away; to mitigate; to excuse.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_4">Etymology 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">salvē</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Interjection">Interjection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>Hail; a greeting.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_5">Etymology 5</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From the interjection <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb_3">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:salve.html>salve</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">salves</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">salving</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">salved</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To say “salve” to; to greet; to salute.
<ul><li><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(Can <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> date this quote by Spenser and provide title, author’s full name, and other <a href = vnd.unilang:details.html>details</a>?)</span>
<dl><dd>By this that stranger knight in presence <a href = vnd.unilang:came.html>came</a>, / And goodly <b>salved</b> them.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
</body>

***sam.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:sam.html>sam</a> (787)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Acronym
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:sam.html>sam</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>surface-to-air missile</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">sammen</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">samnen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">samnian</i>, <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">ġesamnian</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to collect, assemble, bring together, gather, join, unite, compose, meet, glean</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*samnōną</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to gather</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*sem-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">one</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">zamelen</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to collect</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">sammeln</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to collect, gather</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Swedish language">Swedish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sv">samla</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to gather, collect</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Icelandic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Icelandic language">Icelandic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="is">samna</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to gather, collect</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. More at <span class="Latn" lang="en">same</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:sam.html>sam</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">sams</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">samming</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">sammed</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  dialectal</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To assemble.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  dialectal<span class="ib-comma">,</span> of persons</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To bring together; join (in marriage, friendship, love, etc.).</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  dialectal<span class="ib-comma">,</span> of <a href = vnd.unilang:things.html>things</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To bring together; collect; put in order; arrange.
<ul><li><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(Can <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> date this quote by Snowden and provide title, author's full name, and other <a href = vnd.unilang:details.html>details</a>?)</span>
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>We</a> <b>sammed</b> together all <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> could find.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  dialectal</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To assemble; come together.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  dialectal</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To coagulate; curdle (milk).</li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li>Often used with <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">together</i> or <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">up</i></li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">sām</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">together</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href = vnd.unilang:samen.html>samen</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">together</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*samana</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">together</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*sem-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">together, one</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverb">Adverb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<li><b>a1600</b>, <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.ru/books?id=1jcUAAAAYAAJamp;pg=PA97amp;dq=All+Sam+the+soldiers+then+replied.amp;hl=enamp;sa=Xamp;ved=0ahUKEwibsZPo2dXWAhUESJoKHcPoAp0Q6AEIKDAAv=onepageamp;q=All%20Sam%20the%20soldiers%20then%20replied.amp;f=false">The Battle of Floddon Field</a></i>:

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_4">Etymology 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">sam-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="ann-pos">prefix</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">sām-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">half-; partly; incompletely</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*sēmi-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:half.html>half</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*sēmi-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:half.html>half</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Related to <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">semi-</i> (<a href = vnd.unilang:via.html>via</a> <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span>).
</p>

***sambal.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:sambal.html>sambal</a> (88531)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malay_language" class="extiw" title="w:Malay language">Malay</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ms"><a href = vnd.unilang:sambal.html>sambal</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Javanese_language" class="extiw" title="w:Javanese language">Javanese</a></span> <i class="Java mention" lang="jv">ꦱꦩ꧀ꦧꦼꦭ꧀</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="jv-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">sambel</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. In Surinamese Dutch it may have <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> directly borrowed from Javanese, although the meaning <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> rather distinct from the Javanese word.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:sambal.html>sambal</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:sambal.html>sambals</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands" class="extiw" title="w:Netherlands">Netherlands</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgium" class="extiw" title="w:Belgium">Belgium</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> chiefly uncountable</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:sambal.html>Sambal</a></span>, a relish made from <a href = vnd.unilang:chili.html>chili</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:peppers.html>peppers</a>. <span class="defdate">[from late 18th c.]</span>
<ul><li><b>1797</b>, J. S. Stavorinus, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:reizen.html>Reize</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:van.html>van</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zeeland.html>Zeeland</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:kaap.html>Kaap</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:goede.html>Goede</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:hoop.html>Hoop</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:en.html>en</a> Batavia, <a href = vnd.unilang:naar.html>naar</a> Samarang, Macasser, Amboina, Suratte, <a href = vnd.unilang:enz.html>enz</a>.</i>, <a href = vnd.unilang:vol.html>vol</a>. I, publ. by A. amp; J. Honkoop, page 261.

***samen-.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:samen-.html>samen-</a></h1><br><a href = vnd.unilang:co-.html>co-</a>, fellow</br></body> 
***samen.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:samen.html>samen</a> (295)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">tsamen</i>, a contraction of earlier <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:tesamen.html>tesamen</a></i>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:te.html>te</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:samen.html>samen</a></i>. Although not clear from the spelling, the ⟨s⟩ in the Middle Dutch word <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> pronounced as voiced <span class="IPA">/z/</span>. That <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">(<a href = vnd.unilang:te.html>te</a>)<a href = vnd.unilang:samen.html>samen</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> pronounced <span class="IPA">/(tə)zaːmən/</span>, like the modern descendant <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:tezamen.html>tezamen</a></i> and the related <a href = vnd.unilang:words.html>words</a> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:gezamenlijk.html>gezamenlijk</a></i> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:verzamelen.html>verzamelen</a></i>. The contracted form <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">tsamen</i>, however, <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> a voiceless <span class="IPA">/s/</span> because it <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> assimilated to the preceding <span class="IPA">/<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a>/</span>, creating an affricate. This affricate <span class="IPA">/ts/</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:later.html>later</a> simplified to <span class="IPA">/s/</span>.
</p><p>Middle Dutch <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:samen.html>samen</a></i> derives from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">saman</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*samana</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">together</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*sem-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">one, together</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Compare also <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:sommige.html>sommige</a></i> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:soms.html>soms</a></i>, from the zero grade of the same Indo-European root.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverb">Adverb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:samen.html>samen</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>together</li></ol>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bijwoord"><i><a href = vnd.unilang:bijwoord.html>Bijwoord</a></i></span></h4>
